<Name>Todd Harper< /Name><time>1563567205964</time>< Rate>
5</Rate>
<Review>My wife and I are escape room enthusiasts with over 20 rooms under our belts. We try to play at least one game whenever we travel. While we didn't escape from The House of Clues' Alien Spacecraft Invasion (correction: we escaped, but we didn't save the earth), we had a blast! The scenery in the room is awesome, the lights are disorienting (just like they should be on a UFO), and the puzzles are challenging! Plus, there's a surprise waiting in the room that made both me and my wife jump!

My only complaint about this room was the number of similar locks. It's totally a preference thing, but I think a perfect escape room has only one of each type of lock at a time, so when I discover 3 digits or a key, I know exactly where it's supposed to go. Here, I had to test each combination in three or four different locks before finding the right one. That ate a lot of our time.

We had a nice chat with the owner after playing and are very impressed with their business!

Overall, we had an excellent time here and will be returning to play their Pirate Ghost Ship!</Review>< Pictures>

<user_id>108597410149809049716</user_id><time>1530723625569</time>< Review>
First time here and it was amazing. Ive done a handful of other escape rooms and so far this place was the best. The organization of the clues was great and didnt force you into a clueless circle. The puzzles were difficult enough to get you thinking and get creative but easy enough so that you all dont just stand there not knowing what to do next. The props were so much fun to interact with and for at least the room I was in, they didnt try to bog you down with endless red herrings that get you stuck and unable to move forward. The price isnt bad for what it is, I would personally say it is worth paying the 35, load of fun. I cant wait to try another room!< /Review>

< review>
Not bad. Had time to kill. Decided to check this spot. A little bit crowded. But still got seated rather quickly. Service was kind. Pricing was typical. A little overpriced....but we are in LA.

This place is clean. Full bar. Food came out hot. Had pretty nice presentation. The food was also delicious. A lot more flavor than I expected. The drinks were a little basic. I ordered a Makers Whiskey sour. No garnishment. No presentation at all. Wasn't a horrible drink. But wasn't great either.

So for airport food....would I eat here again ? Sure. Why not. Good enough. Bar seating if you like. Television if you wanna catch a game. Not bad.</review>

Ate a quick dinner here before our flight at this restaurant inside Los Angeles Airport. The menu had a lot of good choices such as pizza, hamburgers and a large variety of sandwiches.
I ordered a BLT and French Frys (see photo). The prices were typical of an airport restaurant (always more expensive).  My husband ordered a bowl of Tortilla Soup, which was a fairly small serving size, and the soup was 'okay', but not good enough that he would order again. The service was good, but not great, and that is the reason for my 4 Star Review. The wait staff wasn't  very enthusiastic or friendly. The seating was comfortable,  and the music was pleasant (not too loud like the adjacent 'Rock and Roll' restaurant). Overall, we enjoyed our pre-flight meal at this Airport restaurant.<//Review>

<date>1564606511437</date><Rate>5</Rate><text>Reminder: manage your expectations at a large international airport restaurant.
We were told before we were seated that it would take 20-25 min to receive food once we ordered, and were asked if that would be okay.
Since we had 3 hours to kill before our flight we had no issues.  We recieved great service all around, and did not have to wait long for food.
The drinks we ordered were tasty (Pacific Ocean Punch) as were the burger and fries and pulled pork grilled cheese on brioche.

We got here an hour before closing and their wasn't too many people here so we didn't have to wait to long for the sandwiches to be prepared.
We split Italian pasta salad and that was very good, I liked the fact that it wasn't too overwhelmingly packed with olives and had little cheese pieces. We ordered an Italiano and a Bull both on soft bread. I think I preferred the Bull better since of course it had prosciutto, mozzarella and the red peppers. My only issue was that it has the balsamic vinegar and plenty of mayo, but then again I'm not a big of mayo (or mustard, or pickles lol) but they do mention that on the menu so you can adjust the sandwiches how you like. My sister on the other hand had no problem with they way it way prepared she liked both just fine.
We finished this off with a chocolate mousse, that little cup was really good.

You know just a heads up for next time we come and there will be a next time, the 10' inch is split into 3 pieces that could easily be split with 3 people lol so we might stick to a 6' inch sandwich. I might also try the other bread they have. Staff was really friendly and helpful with their suggestions.<//Review>< pics>

<user_id>118196398821978662050<//user_id><user_name>Rie H<//user_name><date>1525591162974< /date><rate>3</rate><review>Since moving to NorCal from LA, I've been searching for a good ramen place. Generally my preference is the strong flavored tonkotsu ramen.

Parking:
Myzen is located inside a plaza with a decent sized parking lot but because there are so many other shops it might be difficult to find parking during lunch/dinner hours.

Interior:
It's a pretty decent size restaurant and was very clean. There are plenty of tables to fit groups of 4-6 and possibly more.

Staff:
The staff are friendly and attentive. As soon as I closed my menu the server came and took my order.

Food:
I got the Myzen ramen (which is their tonkotsu ramen) and gyoza. The gyoza was average like the kind I could buy from there freezer section of the Japanese market but I would've preferred it to be cooked longer so that the outer skin was more crispy.

The broth of the ramen was lighter than I expected but it had enough flavor to not be bland. The noodles were a good chewy texture and tasted good. Also included were soft boiled egg, a couple very thin slices of chashu, seaweed, kikuraage, bamboo shoots, as green onions. The chashu had a good flavor to it however it was very thinly sliced and were small pieces. It's difficult to justify the totally cost of $18.

Overall it's much better than the other ramen places I've tried in San Jose and can see myself coming back here occasionally.<//review>< pictures>
[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipM3kQLlye_XC6JeVpvnScdLVZwqQIYz2QZK_cDx=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pictures>

1525591162974<//Date>
< rate>
3</rate>
<text>Since moving to NorCal from LA, I've been searching for a good ramen place. Generally my preference is the strong flavored tonkotsu ramen.

Parking:
Myzen is located inside a plaza with a decent sized parking lot but because there are so many other shops it might be difficult to find parking during lunch/dinner hours.

Interior:
It's a pretty decent size restaurant and was very clean. There are plenty of tables to fit groups of 4-6 and possibly more.

Staff:
The staff are friendly and attentive. As soon as I closed my menu the server came and took my order.

Food:
I got the Myzen ramen (which is their tonkotsu ramen) and gyoza. The gyoza was average like the kind I could buy from there freezer section of the Japanese market but I would've preferred it to be cooked longer so that the outer skin was more crispy.

The broth of the ramen was lighter than I expected but it had enough flavor to not be bland. The noodles were a good chewy texture and tasted good. Also included were soft boiled egg, a couple very thin slices of chashu, seaweed, kikuraage, bamboo shoots, as green onions. The chashu had a good flavor to it however it was very thinly sliced and were small pieces. It's difficult to justify the totally cost of $18.

Overall it's much better than the other ramen places I've tried in San Jose and can see myself coming back here occasionally.</text><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipM3kQLlye_XC6JeVpvnScdLVZwqQIYz2QZK_cDx=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pics>< response>

It's always a pleasant experience coming to Myzen to eat some quality ramen! I definitely recommend their Myzen Ramen all the way as it has a rich tonkotsu based broth with all the familiar ramen toppings. Side dishes are also worth ordering as well! Not a huge alcohol buff but seems like they havr a pretty nice selection of beer. The staff is always friendly and very prompt with taking your order as well. I've always had very nice and efficient servers serve me while I am here and my food comes out reasonably quickly so kudos to the staff! All in all, Myzen is gem of a Japanese restaurant tucked away in a quaint location that definitely deserves a visit when you're over on this side of town.</text>

<Text>Alright so,

I will say that I am not usually a fan of ramen. I have never found soup as a meal very filling. But my husband likes ramen and we are very close to this place so I suggested we try it. The first time, we went on a weekday around 7 and were seated immediately. Food came out fast! Within ten minutes of ordering. Though that might just be how it goes on a weekday.

This ramen completely blew my mind! Everything about it is perfect, but the broth is especially tasty. We try to make a trip every few weeks, and we we do, I usually order the original Myzen ramen. It's just so delicious, and combined with an appetizer (they have takoyaki -- my favorite food!) it really fills me up. My husband really enjoys the curry ramen.

Thank you, Myzen. You have earned two loyal customers!</Text>< time>

This small Japanese restaurant that can be hard to find as it's located in a strip mall and faces away from its Lawrence Expressway address.  Access from the Eastbound (headed towards 101) via Titan way is the best way find this place. Beer & saki are available.<//text>

<Review>'m so excited for another ramen place in Sunnyvale!!!!! I found this place from Yelp's weekly review, and promptly came here for dinner. We got here around 5:30 Mon Friday and there was plenty of open tables so we got seated immediately.

We got the Myzen Ramen (tonkatsu) and Curry Ramen. I really like the Myzen Ramen, which had a lot of ingredients, including corn (my fav), so I finished the entire thing including the broth. My husband enjoyed the Curry Ramen but it was a but too strong for drinking the broth. He says he will get the Myzen Ramen next time.

I like the tonkatsu broth here better than Ramen Seas, but I usually get Miso Ramen at Ramen Seas. So I will try the Miso Ramen here next time to compare. However, it's a bit more expensive here than Ramen Seas. The Myzen Ramen was $10.95 and Curry Ramen was $12.95. Might be because they have more ingredients though.</Review></record></dataset><record>

<user>105593270217665985575</user>< user_name>
Dan Galpin<//user_name>
<Time>1466309718270< /Time><Rate>5</Rate>< review>
Tried the Tonkatsu Ramen and the Curry Tonkatsu Ramen.  I thought the salt was well-balanced, but I wouldn't have added more.  Both were nice and creamy, with the Tonkatsu being a brilliant shade of white. There were two thin slices of Chashu that were melt-in-your-mouth delicious.  I did add sesame chili oil to both, which added a nice sesame flavor and a bit of a kick.  The egg was perfectly cooked; it was soft and creamy but not runny.  The noodles were curly and firm.  The Curry was a lovely amalgam of Japanese-style Curry and Tonkatsu, and I'd give it a hearty recommendation to fans of either. Overall, an excellent addition to the Ramen choices in the South Bay.</review>

<rate>1<//rate>< review>
Ok let me start off by saying this ramen is NOT authentic at all. The broth from here is just plain salty. Authentic Tonkotsu broth ramen is supposed to be fatty or at the very least taste like pork, but this place just puts a ton of salt in their broth. I ordered the curry tonkotsu ramen (didn't even taste like much curry or pork) and my boyfriend ordered the Myzen tonkotsu broth (which was extremely over salted). This soup tastes like it was made straight up out of a Shin Ramen packet - except I'd rather have Shin Ramen. Save your money and go somewhere else!</review>
